# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`

# etcd Raft Snapshot Too Old on Node Rejoin

## Your Task

An etcd node fails to rejoin a cluster with 'ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable'. Find the Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that (1) define ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable and (2) implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

72-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented the Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that define `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` and implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Summary of Findings

**Key Files Identified:**

1. **raft/storage.go** - Defines `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` error (lines 36-38)
2. **raft/log.go** - The `snapshot()` function retrieves snapshots and can return the error
3. **raft/raft.go** - The `maybeSendSnapshot()` function handles snapshot sending and checks for the error
4. **server/wal/wal.go** - `ValidSnapshotEntries()` validates snapshots based on hardstate commit index
5. **server/etcdserver/api/snap/snapshotter.go** - `LoadNewestAvailable()` loads valid snapshots
6. **server/etcdserver/api/snap/db.go** - `DBFilePath()` validates snapshot file existence
7. **server/etcdserver/server.go** - Server initialization that loads and recovers from snapshots

**How the Snapshot Availability Check Works:**

The error occurs when a node tries to catch up via snapshot during rejoin, but the snapshot is either:
- Too old (filtered out by `ValidSnapshotEntries` because its index exceeds the committed hardstate)
- Missing from disk (returned as `ErrNoDBSnapshot`)
- Being prepared (returned as `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable`)

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, the dependency chain, and a detailed narrative explanation.

If no such index exists\n143: // in the log, the log's first index is returned.\n144: //\n145: // The index provided MUST be equal to or less than l.lastIndex(). Invalid\n146: // inputs log a warning and the input index is returned.\n147: func (l *raftLog) findConflictByTerm(index uint64, term uint64) uint64 {\n148: \tif li := l.lastIndex(); index > li {\n149: \t\t// NB: such calls should not exist, but since there is a straightfoward\n150: \t\t// way to recover, do it.\n151: \t\t//\n152: \t\t// It is tempting to also check something about the first index, but\n153: \t\t// there is odd behavior with peers that have no log, in which case\n154: \t\t// lastIndex will return zero and firstIndex will return one, which\n155: \t\t// leads to calls with an index of zero into this method.\n156: \t\tl.logger.Warningf(\"index(%d) is out of range [0, lastIndex(%d)] in findConflictByTerm\",\n157: \t\t\tindex, li)\n158: \t\treturn index\n159: \t}\n160: \tfor {\n161: \t\tlogTerm, err := l.term(index)\n162: \t\tif logTerm <= term || err != nil {\n163: \t\t\tbreak\n164: \t\t}\n165: \t\tindex--\n166: \t}\n167: \treturn index\n168: }\n169: \n170: func (l *raftLog) unstableEntries() []pb.Entry {\n171: \tif len(l.unstable.entries) == 0 {\n172: \t\treturn nil\n173: \t}\n174: \treturn l.unstable.entries\n175: }\n176: \n177: // nextEnts returns all the available entries for execution.\n178: // If applied is smaller than the index of snapshot, it returns all committed\n179: // entries after the index of snapshot.\n180: func (l *raftLog) nextEnts() (ents []pb.Entry) {\n181: \toff := max(l.applied+1, l.firstIndex())\n182: \tif l.committed+1 > off {\n183: \t\tents, err := l.slice(off, l.committed+1, l.maxNextEntsSize)\n184: \t\tif err != nil {\n185: \t\t\tl.logger.Panicf(\"unexpected error when getting unapplied entries (%v)\", err)\n186: \t\t}\n187: \t\treturn ents\n188: \t}\n189: \treturn nil\n190: }\n191: \n192: // hasNextEnts returns if there is any available entries for execution. This\n193: // is a fast check without heavy raftLog.slice() in raftLog.nextEnts().\n194: func (l *raftLog) hasNextEnts() bool {\n195: \toff := max(l.applied+1, l.firstIndex())\n196: \treturn l.committed+1 > off\n197: }\n198: \n199: // hasPendingSnapshot returns if there is pending snapshot waiting for applying.\n200: func (l *raftLog) hasPendingSnapshot() bool {\n201: \treturn l.unstable.snapshot != nil && !IsEmptySnap(*l.unstable.snapshot)\n202: }\n203: \n204: func (l *raftLog) snapshot() (pb.Snapshot, error) {\n205: \tif l.unstable.snapshot != nil {\n206: \t\treturn *l.unstable.snapshot, nil\n207: \t}\n208: \treturn l.storage.Snapshot()\n209: }\n210: \n211: func (l *raftLog) firstIndex() uint64 {\n212: \tif i, ok := l.unstable.maybeFirstIndex(); ok {\n213: \t\treturn i\n214: \t}\n215: \tindex, err := l.storage.FirstIndex()\n216: \tif err != nil {\n217: \t\tpanic(err) // TODO(bdarnell)\n218: \t}\n219: \treturn index\n220: }\n221: \n222: func (l *raftLog) lastIndex() uint64 {\n223: \tif i, ok := l.unstable.maybeLastIndex(); ok {\n224: \t\treturn i\n225: \t}\n226: \ti, err := l.storage.LastIndex()\n227: \tif err != nil {\n228: \t\tpanic(err) // TODO(bdarnell)\n229: \t}\n230: \treturn i\n231: ",

This error is returned by the Storage interface when a required snapshot is temporarily unavailable, allowing the Raft state machine to know that storage needs time to prepare the snapshot.\\n\\n2. **Snapshot Retrieval (raft/log.go)**: The snapshot() function (lines 204-209) retrieves snapshots from storage. If the file is missing, it returns ErrNoDBSnapshot, indicating the snapshot cannot be restored.\\n\\n7. **Server Initialization (server/etcdserver/server.go)**: During server startup (lines 485-530), the newEtcdServer function calls ValidSnapshotEntries to get valid snapshots from the WAL, then LoadNewestAvailable to load the newest compatible snapshot. The snapshot is recovered if available, enabling proper node rejoin after outages.\\n\\nThe root cause of 'ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable' during node rejoin occurs when: (1) the snapshot index is older than recent log entries needed for catch-up, (2) the snapshot file is orphaned or missing (ErrNoDBSnapshot), or (3) the snapshot is temporarily being prepared. The ValidSnapshotEntries function's filtering by hardstate commit index is critical - it ensures a node cannot load a snapshot that is newer than its persisted committed state, which would cause the 'snapshot too old' error when the node tries to catch up with newer cluster state.\"\n}\n",
